	<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Köppen climate classification</h1>
	
	<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">
		<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>

<p>The <b>Köppen climate classification</b> is one of the most widely used <a href="/wiki/Climate_classification" title="Climate classification">climate classification</a> systems. It was first published by the German-Russian <a href="/wiki/List_of_climate_scientists" title="List of climate scientists">climatologist</a> <a href="/wiki/Wladimir_K%C3%B6ppen" title="Wladimir Köppen">Wladimir Köppen</a> (1846–1940) in 1884,<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> with several later modifications by Köppen, notably in 1918 and 1936.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> Later, the climatologist <a href="/wiki/Rudolf_Geiger" title="Rudolf Geiger">Rudolf Geiger</a> introduced some changes to the classification system, which is thus sometimes called the <b>Köppen–Geiger climate classification system</b>.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Köppen climate classification divides climates into five main climate groups, with each group being divided based on seasonal precipitation and temperature patterns. The five main groups are <i>A</i> (tropical), <i>B</i> (dry), <i>C</i> (temperate), <i>D</i> (continental), and <i>E</i> (polar). Each group and subgroup is represented by a letter. All climates are assigned a main group (the first letter). All climates except for those in the <i>E</i> group are assigned a seasonal precipitation subgroup (the second letter). For example, <i>Af</i> indicates a <a href="/wiki/Tropical_rainforest_climate" title="Tropical rainforest climate">tropical rainforest climate</a>. The system assigns a temperature subgroup for all groups other than those in the <i>A</i> group, indicated by the third letter for climates in <i>B</i>, <i>C</i>, and <i>D</i>, and the second letter for climates in <i>E</i>. For example, <i>Cfb</i> indicates an <a href="/wiki/Oceanic_climate" title="Oceanic climate">oceanic climate</a> with warm summers as indicated by the ending <i>b</i>. Climates are classified based on specific criteria unique to each climate type.<sup id="cite_ref-kottek2006_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kottek2006-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>As Köppen designed the system based on his experience as a botanist, his main climate groups are based on what types of vegetation grow in a given climate classification region. In addition to identifying climates, the system can be used to analyze ecosystem conditions and identify the main types of vegetation within climates. Due to its link with the plant life of a given region, the system is useful in predicting future changes in plant life within that region.<sup id="cite_ref-Beck_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Beck-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Köppen climate classification system has been further modified, within the <a href="/wiki/Trewartha_climate_classification" title="Trewartha climate classification">Trewartha climate classification</a> system in the middle 1960s (revised in 1980). The Trewartha system sought to create a more refined <a href="/wiki/Middle_latitudes" title="Middle latitudes">middle latitude</a> climate zone, which was one of the criticisms of the Köppen system (the C climate group was too broad).<sup id="cite_ref-McKnight_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-McKnight-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>200–1</span></sup>
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r886049878">.mw-parser-output .tocright{float:right;clear:right;width:auto;background:none;padding:.5em 0 .8em 1.4em;margin-bottom:.5em}.mw-parser-output .tocright-clear-left{clear:left}.mw-parser-output .tocright-clear-both{clear:both}.mw-parser-output .tocright-clear-none{clear:none}</style><div class="tocright" style=""><div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2>Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Overview">Overview</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Overview">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<p><br />
The Köppen climate classification scheme divides climates into five main climate groups: <i>A</i> (tropical), <i>B</i> (dry), <i>C</i> (temperate), <i>D</i> (continental), and <i>E</i> (polar).<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> The second letter indicates the seasonal precipitation type, while the third letter indicates the level of heat.<sup id="cite_ref-hanschen_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hanschen-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> Summers are defined as the 6-month period that is warmer either from April–September and/or October–March while winter is the 6-month period that is cooler.<sup id="cite_ref-Beck_1-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Beck-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Peel_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Peel-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><b>Group A: Tropical climates</b>
</p><p>This type of climate has every month of the year with an average temperature of 18&#160;°C (64.4&#160;°F) or higher, with significant precipitation.<sup id="cite_ref-Beck_1-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Beck-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Peel_10-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Peel-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li><i>Af</i> = <a href="/wiki/Tropical_rainforest_climate" title="Tropical rainforest climate">Tropical rainforest climate</a>; average precipitation of at least 60&#160;mm (2.4&#160;in) in every month.</li>
<li><i>Am</i> = <a href="/wiki/Tropical_monsoon_climate" title="Tropical monsoon climate">Tropical monsoon climate</a>; driest month (which nearly always occurs at or soon after the "winter" solstice for that side of the equator) with precipitation less than 60&#160;mm (2.4&#160;in), but at least <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" alttext="{\textstyle 100-\left({\frac {Total\ Annual\ Precipitation\ (mm)}{25}}\right)}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="false" scriptlevel="0">
        <mn>100</mn>
        <mo>&#x2212;<!-- − --></mo>
        <mrow>
          <mo>(</mo>
          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mfrac>
              <mrow>
                <mi>T</mi>

                <mi>t</mi>

              </mrow>
              <mn>25</mn>
            </mfrac>
          </mrow>

        </mrow>

    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\textstyle 100-\left({\frac {Total\ Annual\ Precipitation\ (mm)}{25}}\right)}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/603c8fdbbab7d84e5380dae2671b4c3b691307ec" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -1.838ex; width:35.083ex; height:4.843ex;" alt="{\textstyle 100-\left({\frac {Total\ Annual\ Precipitation\ (mm)}{25}}\right)}"/></span>.<sup id="cite_ref-Beck_1-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Beck-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Peel_10-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Peel-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><i>Aw</i> or <i>As</i> = Tropical wet and dry or <a href="/wiki/Tropical_savanna_climate" title="Tropical savanna climate">savanna</a> climate; with the driest month having precipitation less than 60&#160;mm (2.4&#160;in) and less than <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" alttext="{\textstyle 100-\left({\frac {Total\ Annual\ Precipitation\ (mm)}{25}}\right)}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="false" scriptlevel="0">
        <mn>100</mn>
        <mo>&#x2212;<!-- − --></mo>
        <mrow>
          <mo>(</mo>
          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mfrac>
              <mrow>
                <mi>T</mi>
                <mi>o</mi>
                <mi>t</mi>
                <mi>a</mi>
                <mi>l</mi>
                <mtext>&#xA0;</mtext>
                <mi>A</mi>
                <mi>n</mi>
                <mi>n</mi>
                <mi>u</mi>
                <mi>a</mi>

                <mtext>&#xA0;</mtext>

                <mi>e</mi>

          </mrow>
          <mo>)</mo>
        </mrow>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\textstyle 100-\left({\frac {Total\ Annual\ Precipitation\ (mm)}{25}}\right)}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/603c8fdbbab7d84e5380dae2671b4c3b691307ec" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -1.838ex; width:35.083ex; height:4.843ex;" alt="{\textstyle 100-\left({\frac {Total\ Annual\ Precipitation\ (mm)}{25}}\right)}"/></span>.<sup id="cite_ref-Beck_1-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Beck-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Peel_10-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Peel-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<p><b>Group B: Dry climates</b>
</p><p>This type of climate is defined by little precipitation.
</p><p>Multiply the average annual temperature in <a href="/wiki/Celsius" title="Celsius">Celsius</a> by 20, then add
</p>
<dl><dd>(a) 280 if 70% or more of the total precipitation is in the spring and summer months (April–September in the Northern Hemisphere, or October–March in the Southern), or</dd>
<dd>(b) 140 if 30%–70% of the total precipitation is received during the spring and summer, or</dd>
<dd>(c) 0 if less than 30% of the total precipitation is received during the spring and summer.</dd></dl>
<p>If the annual precipitation is less than 50% of this threshold, the classification is BW (arid: desert climate); if it is in the range of 50%–100% of the threshold, the classification is BS (semi-arid: steppe climate).<sup id="cite_ref-Beck_1-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Beck-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Peel_10-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Peel-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A third letter can be included to indicate temperature. Originally, h signified low-latitude climate (average annual temperature above 18&#160;°C (64.4&#160;°F)) while k signified middle-latitude climate (average annual temperature below 18&#160;°C), but the more common practice today, especially in the United States, is to use h to mean the coldest month has an average temperature above 0&#160;°C (32&#160;°F) (or −3&#160;°C (27&#160;°F)), with k denoting that at least one month's averages below 0&#160;°C (or −3&#160;°C (27&#160;°F)). The n is used to denote a climate characterized by frequent fog.<sup id="cite_ref-Cereceda_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cereceda-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-gepchile_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gepchile-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Inzunza_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Inzunza-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li><i>BWh</i> = <a href="/wiki/Hot_desert_climate" class="mw-redirect" title="Hot desert climate">Hot desert climate</a></li>
<li><i>BWk</i> = <a href="/wiki/Cold_desert_climate" class="mw-redirect" title="Cold desert climate">Cold desert climate</a></li>
<li><i>BSh</i> = <a href="/wiki/Hot_semi-arid_climate" class="mw-redirect" title="Hot semi-arid climate">Hot semi-arid climate</a></li>
<li><i>BSk</i> = <a href="/wiki/Cold_semi-arid_climate" class="mw-redirect" title="Cold semi-arid climate">Cold semi-arid climate</a></li></ul>
<p><b>Group C: Temperate climates</b>
</p><p>This type of climate has the coldest month averaging between 0&#160;°C (32&#160;°F)<sup id="cite_ref-Peel_10-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Peel-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> (or −3&#160;°C (27&#160;°F))<sup id="cite_ref-kottek2006_8-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kottek2006-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> and 18&#160;°C (64.4&#160;°F) and at least one month averaging above 10&#160;°C (50&#160;°F).<sup id="cite_ref-Peel_10-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Peel-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-kottek2006_8-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kottek2006-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li><i>Cfa</i> = <a href="/wiki/Humid_subtropical_climate" title="Humid subtropical climate">Humid subtropical climate</a>; coldest month averaging above 0&#160;°C (32&#160;°F)  (or −3&#160;°C (27&#160;°F)), at least one month's average temperature above 22&#160;°C (71.6&#160;°F), and at least four months averaging above 10&#160;°C (50&#160;°F). No significant precipitation difference between seasons (neither abovementioned set of conditions fulfilled). No dry months in the summer.</li>
<li><i>Cfb</i> = Temperate <a href="/wiki/Oceanic_climate" title="Oceanic climate">oceanic climate</a>; coldest month averaging above 0&#160;°C (32&#160;°F) (or −3&#160;°C (27&#160;°F)), all months with average temperatures below 22&#160;°C (71.6&#160;°F), and at least four months averaging above 10&#160;°C (50&#160;°F). No significant precipitation difference between seasons (neither abovementioned set of conditions fulfilled).</li>
<li><i>Cfc</i> = <a href="/wiki/Subpolar_oceanic_climate" class="mw-redirect" title="Subpolar oceanic climate">Subpolar oceanic climate</a>; coldest month averaging above 0&#160;°C (32&#160;°F)  (or −3&#160;°C (27&#160;°F)) and 1–3 months averaging above 10&#160;°C (50&#160;°F). No significant precipitation difference between seasons (neither abovementioned set of conditions fulfilled).</li>
<li><i>Cwa</i> = <a href="/wiki/Monsoon" title="Monsoon">Monsoon</a>-influenced humid subtropical climate; coldest month averaging above 0&#160;°C (32&#160;°F)  (or −3&#160;°C (27&#160;°F)), at least one month's average temperature above 22&#160;°C (71.6&#160;°F), and at least four months averaging above 10&#160;°C (50&#160;°F). At least ten times as much rain in the wettest month of summer as in the driest month of winter (alternative definition is 70% or more of average annual precipitation is received in the warmest six months).</li>
<li><i>Cwb</i> = <a href="/wiki/Subtropical_highland_climate" class="mw-redirect" title="Subtropical highland climate">Subtropical highland climate</a> or Monsoon-influenced temperate oceanic climate; coldest month averaging above 0&#160;°C (32&#160;°F) (or −3&#160;°C (27&#160;°F)), all months with average temperatures below 22&#160;°C (71.6&#160;°F), and at least four months averaging above 10&#160;°C (50&#160;°F). At least ten times as much rain in the wettest month of summer as in the driest month of winter (an alternative definition is 70% or more of average annual precipitation received in the warmest six months).</li>
<li><i>Cwc</i> = Cold <a href="/wiki/Subtropical_highland_climate" class="mw-redirect" title="Subtropical highland climate">subtropical highland climate</a> or Monsoon-influenced subpolar oceanic climate; coldest month averaging above 0&#160;°C (32&#160;°F) (or −3&#160;°C (27&#160;°F)) and 1–3 months averaging above 10&#160;°C (50&#160;°F). At least ten times as much rain in the wettest month of summer as in the driest month of winter (alternative definition is 70% or more of average annual precipitation is received in the warmest six months).</li>
<li><i>Csa</i> = <a href="/wiki/Hot-summer_Mediterranean_climate" class="mw-redirect" title="Hot-summer Mediterranean climate">Hot-summer Mediterranean climate</a>; coldest month averaging above 0&#160;°C (32&#160;°F)  (or −3&#160;°C (27&#160;°F)), at least one month's average temperature above 22&#160;°C (71.6&#160;°F), and at least four months averaging above 10&#160;°C (50&#160;°F). At least three times as much precipitation in the wettest month of winter as in the driest month of summer, and driest month of summer receives less than 30&#160;mm (1.2&#160;in).</li>
<li><i>Csb</i> = <a href="/wiki/Warm-summer_Mediterranean_climate" class="mw-redirect" title="Warm-summer Mediterranean climate">Warm-summer Mediterranean climate</a>; coldest month averaging above 0&#160;°C (32&#160;°F) (or −3&#160;°C (27&#160;°F)), all months with average temperatures below 22&#160;°C (71.6&#160;°F), and at least four months averaging above 10&#160;°C (50&#160;°F). At least three times as much precipitation in the wettest month of winter as in the driest month of summer, and driest month of summer receives less than 30&#160;mm (1.2&#160;in).</li>
<li><i>Csc</i> = <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_climate#Cold-summer_Mediterranean_climate" title="Mediterranean climate">Cold-summer Mediterranean climate</a>; coldest month averaging above 0&#160;°C (32&#160;°F) (or −3&#160;°C (27&#160;°F)) and 1–3 months averaging above 10&#160;°C (50&#160;°F). At least three times as much precipitation in the wettest month of winter as in the driest month of summer, and driest month of summer receives less than 30&#160;mm (1.2&#160;in).</li></ul>
<p><b>Group D: Continental climates</b>
</p><p>This type of climate has at least one month averaging below 0&#160;°C (32&#160;°F) (or −3&#160;°C (27&#160;°F)) and at least one month averaging above 10&#160;°C (50&#160;°F).<sup id="cite_ref-Peel_10-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Peel-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-kottek2006_8-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kottek2006-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li><i>Dfa</i> = Hot-summer <a href="/wiki/Humid_continental_climate" title="Humid continental climate">humid continental climate</a>; coldest month averaging below −0&#160;°C (32&#160;°F) (or −3&#160;°C (27&#160;°F)), at least one month's average temperature above 22&#160;°C (71.6&#160;°F), and at least four months averaging above 10&#160;°C (50&#160;°F). No significant precipitation difference between seasons (neither abovementioned set of conditions fulfilled).</li>
<li><i>Dfb</i> = Warm-summer <a href="/wiki/Humid_continental_climate" title="Humid continental climate">humid continental climate</a>; coldest month averaging below −0&#160;°C (32&#160;°F) (or −3&#160;°C (27&#160;°F)), all months with average temperatures below 22&#160;°C (71.6&#160;°F), and at least four months averaging above 10&#160;°C (50&#160;°F). No significant precipitation difference between seasons (neither abovementioned set of conditions fulfilled).</li>
<li><i>Dfc</i> = <a href="/wiki/Subarctic_climate" title="Subarctic climate">Subarctic climate</a>; coldest month averaging below 0&#160;°C (32&#160;°F) (or −3&#160;°C (27&#160;°F))  and 1–3 months averaging above 10&#160;°C (50&#160;°F). No significant precipitation difference between seasons (neither abovementioned set of conditions fulfilled).</li>
<li><i>Dfd</i> = Extremely cold subarctic climate; coldest month averaging below −38&#160;°C (−36.4&#160;°F) and 1–3 months averaging above 10&#160;°C (50&#160;°F). No significant precipitation difference between seasons (neither abovementioned set of conditions fulfilled).</li>
<li><i>Dwa</i> = Monsoon-influenced hot-summer humid continental climate; coldest month averaging below 0&#160;°C (32&#160;°F) (or −3&#160;°C (27&#160;°F)), at least one month's average temperature above 22&#160;°C (71.6&#160;°F), and at least four months averaging above 10&#160;°C (50&#160;°F). At least ten times as much rain in the wettest month of summer as in the driest month of winter (alternative definition is 70% or more of average annual precipitation is received in the warmest six months).</li>
<li><i>Dwb</i> = Monsoon-influenced warm-summer humid continental climate; coldest month averaging below 0&#160;°C (32&#160;°F) (or −3&#160;°C (27&#160;°F)), all months with average temperatures below 22&#160;°C (71.6&#160;°F), and at least four months averaging above 10&#160;°C (50&#160;°F). At least ten times as much rain in the wettest month of summer as in the driest month of winter (alternative definition is 70% or more of average annual precipitation is received in the warmest six months).</li>
<li><i>Dwc</i> = Monsoon-influenced <a href="/wiki/Subarctic_climate" title="Subarctic climate">subarctic climate</a>; coldest month averaging below 0&#160;°C (32&#160;°F) (or −3&#160;°C (27&#160;°F))  and 1–3 months averaging above 10&#160;°C (50&#160;°F). At least ten times as much rain in the wettest month of summer as in the driest month of winter (alternative definition is 70% or more of average annual precipitation is received in the warmest six months).</li>
<li><i>Dwd</i> = Monsoon-influenced extremely cold <a href="/wiki/Subarctic_climate" title="Subarctic climate">subarctic climate</a>; coldest month averaging below −38&#160;°C (−36.4&#160;°F) and 1–3 months averaging above 10&#160;°C (50&#160;°F). At least ten times as much rain in the wettest month of summer as in the driest month of winter (alternative definition is 70% or more of average annual precipitation is received in the warmest six months).</li>
<li><i>Dsa</i> = <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_climate" title="Mediterranean climate">Mediterranean</a>-influenced hot-summer humid continental climate; coldest month averaging below 0&#160;°C (32&#160;°F) (or −3&#160;°C (27&#160;°F)), average temperature of the warmest month above 22&#160;°C (71.6&#160;°F) and at least four months averaging above 10&#160;°C (50&#160;°F). At least three times as much precipitation in the wettest month of winter as in the driest month of summer, and driest month of summer receives less than 30&#160;mm (1.2&#160;in).</li>
<li><i>Dsb</i> = Mediterranean-influenced warm-summer humid continental climate; coldest month averaging below 0&#160;°C (32&#160;°F) (or −3&#160;°C (27&#160;°F)), average temperature of the warmest month below 22&#160;°C (71.6&#160;°F) and at least four months averaging above 10&#160;°C (50&#160;°F). At least three times as much precipitation in the wettest month of winter as in the driest month of summer, and driest month of summer receives less than 30&#160;mm (1.2&#160;in).</li>
<li><i>Dsc</i> = Mediterranean-influenced subarctic climate; coldest month averaging below 0&#160;°C (32&#160;°F) (or −3&#160;°C (27&#160;°F))  and 1–3 months averaging above 10&#160;°C (50&#160;°F). At least three times as much precipitation in the wettest month of winter as in the driest month of summer, and driest month of summer receives less than 30&#160;mm (1.2&#160;in).</li>
<li><i>Dsd</i> = Mediterranean-influenced extremely cold subarctic climate; coldest month averaging below −38&#160;°C (−36.4&#160;°F) and 1–3 months averaging above 10&#160;°C (50&#160;°F). At least three times as much precipitation in the wettest month of winter as in the driest month of summer, and driest month of summer receives less than 30&#160;mm (1.2&#160;in).</li></ul>
<p><b>Group E: Polar and alpine climates</b>
</p><p>This type of climate has every month of the year with an average temperature below 10&#160;°C (50&#160;°F).<sup id="cite_ref-Beck_1-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Beck-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Peel_10-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Peel-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li><i>ET</i> = <a href="/wiki/Tundra" title="Tundra">Tundra</a> climate; average temperature of warmest month between 0&#160;°C (32&#160;°F) and 10&#160;°C (50&#160;°F).<sup id="cite_ref-Beck_1-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Beck-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Peel_10-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Peel-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><i>EF</i> = <a href="/wiki/Ice_cap_climate" title="Ice cap climate">Ice cap climate</a>; eternal winter, with all 12 months of the year with average temperatures below 0&#160;°C (32&#160;°F).<sup id="cite_ref-Beck_1-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Beck-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Peel_10-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Peel-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<h2><span id="Group_A:_Tropical.2Fmegathermal_climates"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Group_A:_Tropical/megathermal_climates">Group A: Tropical/megathermal climates</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Group A: Tropical/megathermal climates">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p><a href="/wiki/Tropical_climate" title="Tropical climate">Tropical climates</a> are characterized by constant high temperatures (at sea level and low elevations); all 12 months of the year have average temperatures of 18&#160;°C (64.4&#160;°F)  or higher. They are subdivided as follows:
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Af:_Tropical_rainforest_climate"><i>Af</i>: Tropical rainforest climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Af: Tropical rainforest climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tropical_rainforest_climate" title="Tropical rainforest climate">Tropical rainforest climate</a></div>
<p>All 12 months have an average precipitation of at least 60&#160;mm (2.4&#160;in). These climates usually occur within 10° latitude of the <a href="/wiki/Equator" title="Equator">equator</a>. This climate has no natural seasons in terms of thermal and moisture changes.<sup id="cite_ref-McKnight_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-McKnight-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> When it is dominated most of the year by the <a href="/wiki/Doldrums" class="mw-redirect" title="Doldrums">doldrums</a> low-pressure system due to the presence of the <a href="/wiki/Intertropical_Convergence_Zone" title="Intertropical Convergence Zone">Intertropical Convergence Zone</a> (ITCZ) and when they are no cyclones then the climate is qualified as equatorial. When the trade winds are dominant most of the year, the climate is a tropical trade-wind rainforest climate.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><b>Examples</b>
</p>
<div>
<div>

&#32;
<table class="multicol" role="presentation" style="border-collapse: collapse; padding: 0; border: 0; background:transparent; width:70%;"><tbody><tr>
<td style="width: 50%;text-align: left; vertical-align: top;">

<li><a href="/wiki/Balikpapan" title="Balikpapan">Balikpapan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesia</a> (<i>Af</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Davao_City" title="Davao City">Davao</a>, <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a> (<i>Af</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Georgetown,_Guyana" title="Georgetown, Guyana">Georgetown</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guyana" title="Guyana">Guyana</a> (<i>Af</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Hilo,_Hawaii" title="Hilo, Hawaii">Hilo, Hawaii</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> (<i>Af</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Honiara" title="Honiara">Honiara</a>, <a href="/wiki/Solomon_Islands" title="Solomon Islands">Solomon Islands</a> (<i>Af</i>)</li>

<li><a href="/wiki/Kuching" title="Kuching">Kuching</a>, Malaysia (<i>Af</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Lae" title="Lae">Lae</a>, <a href="/wiki/Papua_New_Guinea" title="Papua New Guinea">Papua New Guinea</a> (<i>Af</i>)</li></ul>
<p>&#32;
</p>
</td>
<td style="width: 50%;text-align: left; vertical-align: top;">
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Medan" title="Medan">Medan</a>, Indonesia (<i>Af</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Moroni,_Comoros" title="Moroni, Comoros">Moroni</a>, <a href="/wiki/Comoros" title="Comoros">Comoros</a> (<i>Af</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Paramaribo" title="Paramaribo">Paramaribo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Suriname" title="Suriname">Suriname</a> (<i>Af</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Pontianak,_Indonesia" class="mw-redirect" title="Pontianak, Indonesia">Pontianak</a>, Indonesia (<i>Af</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Quibd%C3%B3" title="Quibdó">Quibdó</a>, Colombia (<i>Af</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ratnapura" title="Ratnapura">Ratnapura</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sri_Lanka" title="Sri Lanka">Sri Lanka</a> (<i>Af</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Salvador_da_Bahia" class="mw-redirect" title="Salvador da Bahia">Salvador da Bahia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a> (<i>Af</i>)</li>

<li><a href="/wiki/Singapore" title="Singapore">Singapore</a> (<i>Af</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Suva" title="Suva">Suva</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fiji" title="Fiji">Fiji</a> (<i>Af</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Toamasina" title="Toamasina">Toamasina</a>, <a href="/wiki/Madagascar" title="Madagascar">Madagascar</a> (<i>Af</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Victoria,_Seychelles" title="Victoria, Seychelles">Victoria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Seychelles" title="Seychelles">Seychelles</a> (<i>Af</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/West_Palm_Beach,_Florida" title="West Palm Beach, Florida">West Palm Beach, Florida</a>, United States (<i>Af</i>)</li></ul>
<p>&#32;
</p>
</td></tr></tbody></table></div>
</div>
<p>Some of the places with this climate are indeed uniformly and monotonously wet throughout the year (e.g., the northwest <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Ocean" title="Pacific Ocean">Pacific</a> coast of <a href="/wiki/South_America" title="South America">South</a> and <a href="/wiki/Central_America" title="Central America">Central America</a>, from <a href="/wiki/Ecuador" title="Ecuador">Ecuador</a> to <a href="/wiki/Costa_Rica" title="Costa Rica">Costa Rica</a>; see, for instance, <a href="/wiki/Andagoya" title="Andagoya">Andagoya</a>, <a href="/wiki/Colombia" title="Colombia">Colombia</a>), but in many cases, the period of higher sun and longer days is distinctly wettest (as at <a href="/wiki/Palembang" title="Palembang">Palembang</a>, <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesia</a>) or the time of lower sun and shorter days may have more rain (as at <a href="/wiki/Sitiawan" title="Sitiawan">Sitiawan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Malaysia" title="Malaysia">Malaysia</a>).
Among these places some have a pure equatorial climate (Balikpapan, Kuala Lumpur, Kuching, Lae, Medan, Paramaribo, Pontianak and Singapore) with the dominant ITCZ aerological mechanism and no cyclones or a subequatorial climate with occasional cyclones (Davao, Ratnapura, Victoria).
</p><p>(<b>Note</b>. The term <a href="/wiki/Season" title="Season">aseasonal</a> refers to the lack in the tropical zone of large differences in daylight hours and mean monthly (or daily) temperature throughout the year. Annual cyclic changes occur in the tropics, but not as predictably as those in the temperate zone, albeit unrelated to temperature, but to water availability whether as rain, mist, soil, or ground water. Plant response (e. g., <a href="/wiki/Phenology" title="Phenology">phenology</a>), animal (feeding, migration, reproduction, etc.), and human activities (plant sowing, harvesting, hunting, fishing, etc.) are tuned to this 'seasonality'. Indeed, in tropical South America and Central America, the 'rainy season' (and the 'high water season') is called <a href="/wiki/Rainy_season" class="mw-redirect" title="Rainy season"><i>invierno</i></a> or <i>inverno</i>, though it could occur in the Northern Hemisphere summer; likewise, the 'dry season' (and 'low water season') is called <a href="/wiki/Dry_season" title="Dry season"><i>verano</i></a> or <i>verão</i>, and can occur in the Northern Hemisphere winter).
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Am:_Tropical_monsoon_climate"><i>Am</i>: Tropical monsoon climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Am: Tropical monsoon climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tropical_monsoon_climate" title="Tropical monsoon climate">Tropical monsoon climate</a></div>
<p>This type of climate results from the <a href="/wiki/Monsoon" title="Monsoon">monsoon</a> winds which change direction according to the seasons. This climate has a driest month (which nearly always occurs at or soon after the "winter" solstice for that side of the equator) with rainfall less than 60&#160;mm (2.4&#160;in), but at least <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" alttext="{\textstyle 100-\left({\frac {Total\ Annual\ Precipitation\ (mm)}{25}}\right)}">

</p><p><b>Examples</b>
</p>
<div>
<div>

&#32;
<table class="multicol" role="presentation" style="border-collapse: collapse; padding: 0; border: 0; background:transparent; width:70%;"><tbody><tr>
<td style="width: 50%;text-align: left; vertical-align: top;">
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Cairns" title="Cairns">Cairns</a>, <a href="/wiki/Queensland" title="Queensland">Queensland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a> (<i>Am</i>)<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Chittagong,_Bangladesh" class="mw-redirect" title="Chittagong, Bangladesh">Chittagong</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bangladesh" title="Bangladesh">Bangladesh</a> (<i>Am</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Coatzacoalcos" title="Coatzacoalcos">Coatzacoalcos</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">Mexico</a> (<i>Am</i>)</li>

<h3><span id="Aw.2FAs:_Tropical_savanna_climate"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Aw/As:_Tropical_savanna_climate"><i>Aw/As</i>: Tropical savanna climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Aw/As: Tropical savanna climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tropical_savanna_climate" title="Tropical savanna climate">Tropical savanna climate</a></div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Aw:_Tropical_savanna_climate_with_non-seasonal_or_dry-winter_characteristics"><i>Aw</i>: Tropical savanna climate with non-seasonal or dry-winter characteristics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Aw: Tropical savanna climate with non-seasonal or dry-winter characteristics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p><i>Aw</i> climates have a pronounced dry season, with the driest month having precipitation less than 60&#160;mm (2.4&#160;in) and less than <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" alttext="{\textstyle 100-\left({\frac {Total\ Annual\ Precipitation\ (mm)}{25}}\right)}">

</div>
<p>Most places that have this climate are found at the outer margins of the <a href="/wiki/Tropical" class="mw-redirect" title="Tropical">tropical</a> zone from the low teens to the mid-20s latitudes, but occasionally an inner-tropical location (e.g., <a href="/wiki/San_Marcos,_Antioquia" title="San Marcos, Antioquia">San Marcos, Antioquia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Colombia" title="Colombia">Colombia</a>) also qualifies. Actually, the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_sea" class="mw-redirect" title="Caribbean sea">Caribbean</a> coast, eastward from the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Urab%C3%A1" title="Gulf of Urabá">Gulf of Urabá</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Colombia" title="Colombia">Colombia</a>–<a href="/wiki/Panam%C3%A1" class="mw-redirect" title="Panamá">Panamá</a> border to the <a href="/wiki/Orinoco_River" class="mw-redirect" title="Orinoco River">Orinoco River</a> delta, on the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">Atlantic Ocean</a> (about 4,000&#160;km), have long dry periods (the extreme is the <i>BSh</i> climate (see below), characterised by very low, unreliable precipitation, present, for instance, in extensive areas in the <a href="https://es.wikipedia.org/wiki/Guajira_Pen%C3%ADnsula" class="extiw" title="es:Guajira Península">Guajira</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Coro_region" title="Coro region">Coro</a>, western <a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">Venezuela</a>, the northernmost peninsulas in South America, which receive &lt;300&#160;mm total annual precipitation, practically all in two or three months).
</p><p>This condition extends to the <a href="/wiki/Lesser_Antilles" title="Lesser Antilles">Lesser Antilles</a> and <a href="/wiki/Greater_Antilles" title="Greater Antilles">Greater Antilles</a> forming the circum-Caribbean dry belt. The length and severity of the dry season diminishes inland (southward); at the latitude of the Amazon River—which flows eastward, just south of the <a href="/wiki/Equator" title="Equator">equatorial</a> line—the climate is <i>Af</i>. East from the <a href="/wiki/Andes" title="Andes">Andes</a>, between the dry, arid Caribbean and the ever-wet Amazon are the Orinoco River's <a href="/wiki/Los_Llanos,_Venezuela" class="mw-redirect" title="Los Llanos, Venezuela">llanos</a> or <a href="/wiki/Savanna" title="Savanna">savannas</a>, from where this climate takes its name.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="As:_Tropical_savanna_climate_with_dry-summer_characteristics"><i>As</i>: Tropical savanna climate with dry-summer characteristics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: As: Tropical savanna climate with dry-summer characteristics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Sometimes <i>As</i> is used in place of <i>Aw</i> if the dry season occurs during the time of higher sun and longer days (during summer).<sup id="cite_ref-kottek2006_8-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kottek2006-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-nwskoppen_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nwskoppen-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> This is the case in parts of <a href="/wiki/Hawaii" title="Hawaii">Hawaii</a>, northwestern Dominican Republic, East Africa, and the Brazilian Northeastern Coast. In most places that have tropical wet and dry climates, however, the dry season occurs during the time of lower sun and shorter days because of <a href="/wiki/Rain_shadow" title="Rain shadow">rain shadow</a> effects during the 'high-sun' part of the year.
</p><p><b>Examples</b>
</p>
<div>
<div>

&#32;
<table class="multicol" role="presentation" style="border-collapse: collapse; padding: 0; border: 0; background:transparent; width:70%;"><tbody><tr>
<td style="width: 50%;text-align: left; vertical-align: top;">
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Lanai_City,_Hawaii" title="Lanai City, Hawaii">Lanai City, Hawaii</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> (<i>As</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/M%C3%A9rida,_Yucat%C3%A1n" title="Mérida, Yucatán">Mérida</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">Mexico</a> (<i>As</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/San_Pedro_Sula" title="San Pedro Sula">San Pedro Sula</a>, <a href="/wiki/Honduras" title="Honduras">Honduras</a> (<i>As</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Monte_Cristi_(Dominican_Republic)" class="mw-redirect" title="Monte Cristi (Dominican Republic)">Monte Cristi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dominican_Republic" title="Dominican Republic">Dominican Republic</a> (<i>As</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Cali" title="Cali">Cali</a>, <a href="/wiki/Colombia" title="Colombia">Colombia</a> (<i>As</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Barranquilla" title="Barranquilla">Barranquilla</a>, <a href="/wiki/Colombia" title="Colombia">Colombia</a> (<i>As</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Matur%C3%ADn" title="Maturín">Maturín</a>, <a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">Venezuela</a> (<i>As</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Port_of_Spain" title="Port of Spain">Port of Spain</a>, <a href="/wiki/Trinidad_and_Tobago" title="Trinidad and Tobago">Trinidad and Tobago</a> (<i>As</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Natal,_Rio_Grande_do_Norte" title="Natal, Rio Grande do Norte">Natal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a> (<i>As</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Fortaleza" title="Fortaleza">Fortaleza</a>, Brazil (<i>As</i>)</li></ul>
<p>&#32;
</p>
</td>
<td style="width: 50%;text-align: left; vertical-align: top;">
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Lu%C3%ADs,_Maranh%C3%A3o" title="São Luís, Maranhão">São Luís</a>, Brazil (<i>As, bordering on Am</i>)</li>

<h2><span id="Group_B:_Dry_.28desert_and_semi-arid.29_climates"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Group_B:_Dry_(desert_and_semi-arid)_climates">Group B: Dry (desert and semi-arid) climates</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Group B: Dry (desert and semi-arid) climates">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Desert_climate" title="Desert climate">Desert climate</a> and <a href="/wiki/Semi-arid_climate" title="Semi-arid climate">Semi-arid climate</a></div>
<p>These climates are characterized by actual precipitation less than a threshold value set equal to the <a href="/wiki/Potential_evapotranspiration" class="mw-redirect" title="Potential evapotranspiration">potential evapotranspiration</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-McKnight_9-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-McKnight-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>212</span></sup> The threshold value (in millimeters) is determined as:
</p><p>Multiply the average annual temperature in °C by 20, then add (a) 280 if 70% or more of the total precipitation is in the high-sun half of the year (April through September in the Northern Hemisphere, or October through March in the Southern), or (b) 140 if 30%–70% of the total precipitation is received during the applicable period, or (c) 0 if less than 30% of the total precipitation is so received.
</p><p>According to the modified Köppen classification system used by modern climatologists, total precipitation in the warmest six months of the year is taken as reference instead of the total precipitation in the high-sun half of the year.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>If the annual precipitation is less than 50% of this threshold, the classification is <i>BW</i> (arid: <a href="/wiki/Desert_climate" title="Desert climate">desert climate</a>); if it is in the range of 50%–100% of the threshold, the classification is <i>BS</i> (semi-arid: <a href="/wiki/Semi-arid_climate" title="Semi-arid climate">steppe climate</a>).
</p><p>A third letter can be included to indicate temperature. Originally, <i>h</i> signified low-latitude climate (average annual temperature above 18&#160;°C) while <i>k</i> signified middle-latitude climate (average annual temperature below 18&#160;°C), but the more common practice today, especially in the United States, is to use <i>h</i> to mean the coldest month has an average temperature above 0&#160;°C (32&#160;°F) (or −3&#160;°C (27&#160;°F)), with <i>k</i> denoting that at least one month averages below 0&#160;°C.
</p><p>Desert areas situated along the west coasts of continents at tropical or near-tropical locations characterized by <a href="/wiki/Fog_desert" title="Fog desert">frequent fog</a> and low clouds, despite the fact that these places rank among the driest on earth in terms of actual precipitation received are labelled <i>BWn</i> with the n denoting a climate characterized by frequent fog.<sup id="cite_ref-Cereceda_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cereceda-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-gepchile_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gepchile-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Inzunza_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Inzunza-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> The <i>BSn</i> category can be found in foggy coastal steppes.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="BW:_Arid_Climate"><i>BW</i>: Arid Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: BW: Arid Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<h2><span id="Group_C:_Temperate.2Fmesothermal_climates"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Group_C:_Temperate/mesothermal_climates">Group C: Temperate/mesothermal climates</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Group C: Temperate/mesothermal climates">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p><span id="Group_C"></span>
</p>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Temperate_climate" title="Temperate climate">Temperate climate</a></div>
<p>In the Koppen climate system, temperate climates are defined as having an average temperature above 0&#160;°C (32&#160;°F) (or −3&#160;°C (26.6&#160;°F), as noted previously) in their coldest month but below 18&#160;°C (64.4&#160;°F). The average temperature of −3&#160;°C (26.6&#160;°F) roughly coincides with the equatorward limit of frozen ground and snowcover lasting for a month or more.
</p><p>The second letter indicates the precipitation pattern—<i>w</i> indicates dry winters (driest winter month average precipitation less than one-tenth wettest summer month average precipitation. <i>s</i> indicates at least three times as much rain in the wettest month of winter as in the driest month of summer. <i>f</i> means significant precipitation in all seasons (neither above-mentioned set of conditions fulfilled).<sup id="cite_ref-Beck_1-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Beck-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The third letter indicates the degree of summer heat—<i>a</i> indicates warmest month average temperature above 22&#160;°C (71.6&#160;°F) while  <i>b</i> indicates warmest month averaging below 22&#160;°C but with at least four months averaging above 10&#160;°C (50.0&#160;°F), and <i>c</i> indicates one to three months averaging above 10&#160;°C (50.0&#160;°F).<sup id="cite_ref-Beck_1-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Beck-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Peel_10-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Peel-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-kottek2006_8-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kottek2006-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Csa:_Mediterranean_hot_summer_climates"><i>Csa</i>: Mediterranean hot summer climates</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Csa: Mediterranean hot summer climates">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_climate" title="Mediterranean climate">Mediterranean climate</a></div>
<p>These climates usually occur on the western sides of continents between the latitudes of 30° and 45°.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> These climates are in the polar front region in winter, and thus have moderate temperatures and changeable, rainy weather. Summers are hot and dry, due to the domination of the subtropical high pressure systems, except in the immediate coastal areas, where summers are milder due to the nearby presence of cold ocean currents that may bring <a href="/wiki/Fog" title="Fog">fog</a> but prevent rain.<sup id="cite_ref-McKnight_9-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-McKnight-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>221–3</span></sup>
</p><p><b>Examples</b>

<h3><span id="Csb:_Mediterranean_warm.2Fcool_summer_climates"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Csb:_Mediterranean_warm/cool_summer_climates"><i>Csb</i>: Mediterranean warm/cool summer climates</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Csb: Mediterranean warm/cool summer climates">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Dry-summer climates sometimes extend to additional areas (sometimes well north or south of) typical Mediterranean climates, however since their warmest month average temperatures do not reach 22&#160;°C (71.6&#160;°F) they are classified as <i>Csb</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-Beck_1-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Beck-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> Some of these areas would border the <a href="/wiki/Oceanic_climate" title="Oceanic climate">oceanic climate</a> (<i>Cfb</i>), except their dry-summer patterns meet Köppen's <i>Cs</i> minimum thresholds.
</p><p><b>Examples</b>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Csc:_Mediterranean_cold_summer_climates"><i>Csc</i>: Mediterranean cold summer climates</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Csc: Mediterranean cold summer climates">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Cold summer Mediterranean climates (<i>Csc</i>) exist in high-elevation areas adjacent to coastal <i>Csb</i> climate areas, where the strong maritime influence prevents the average winter monthly temperature from dropping below 0&#160;°C. This climate is rare and is predominantly found in climate fringes and isolated areas of the Cascades and Andes Mountains, as the dry-summer climate extends further poleward in the Americas than elsewhere.<sup id="cite_ref-McKnight_9-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-McKnight-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> Rare instances of this climate can be found in some coastal locations in the North Atlantic and at high altitudes in Hawaii.
</p><p><b>Examples</b>
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Akureyri" title="Akureyri">Akureyri</a>, <a href="/wiki/Iceland" title="Iceland">Iceland</a> (<i>Csc</i>), alternatively: dry-summer subarctic climate (<i>Dsc</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Balmaceda,_Chile" title="Balmaceda, Chile">Balmaceda</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chile" title="Chile">Chile</a> (<i>Csc</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Haleakal%C4%81" title="Haleakalā">Haleakalā</a> Summit, <a href="/wiki/Hawaii" title="Hawaii">Hawaii</a>, United States (<i>Csc</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Harstad" title="Harstad">Harstad</a>, <a href="/wiki/Norway" title="Norway">Norway</a> (<i>Csc</i>), alternatively: dry-summer subarctic climate (<i>Dsc</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Liawenee" title="Liawenee">Liawenee</a>, <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a> (<i>Csc, bordering on Csb</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Spirit_Lake_(Washington)" title="Spirit Lake (Washington)">Spirit Lake</a>, <a href="/wiki/Washington_(state)" title="Washington (state)">Washington</a>, United States (<i>Csc</i>)</li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cfa:_Humid_subtropical_climates"><i>Cfa</i>: Humid subtropical climates</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Cfa: Humid subtropical climates">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Humid_subtropical_climate" title="Humid subtropical climate">Humid subtropical climate</a></div>
<p>These climates usually occur on the eastern coasts and eastern sides of continents, usually in the high 20s and 30s latitudes. Unlike the dry summer Mediterranean climates, humid subtropical climates have a warm and wet flow from the tropics that creates warm and moist conditions in the summer months. As such, summer (not winter as is the case in Mediterranean climates) is often the wettest season.
</p><p>The flow out of the subtropical highs and the summer monsoon creates a southerly flow from the tropics that brings warm and moist air to the lower east sides of continents. This flow is often what brings the frequent but short-lived summer thundershowers so typical of the more southerly subtropical  climates like the southern United States, southern China and Japan.<sup id="cite_ref-McKnight_9-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-McKnight-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>223–6</span></sup>
</p><p><b>Examples</b>
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cfb:_Oceanic_climate"><i>Cfb</i>: Oceanic climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Cfb: Oceanic climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Marine_west_coast_climate">Marine west coast climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Marine west coast climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Oceanic_climate" title="Oceanic climate">Oceanic climate</a></div>
<p><i>Cfb</i> climates usually occur in the higher middle latitudes on the western sides of continents between the latitudes of 40° and 60°; they are typically situated immediately poleward of the Mediterranean climates, although in Australia and extreme southern Africa this climate is found immediately poleward of temperate climates, and at a somewhat lower latitude. In western Europe, this climate occurs in coastal areas up to 63°N in Norway.
</p><p>These climates are dominated all year round by the polar front, leading to changeable, often overcast weather. Summers are mild due to cool ocean currents, although hotter, stable weather patterns can set in for periods of time, typically longer at the lower latitude range in the northern hemisphere. Winters are milder than other climates in similar latitudes, but usually very cloudy however not always wet. <i>Cfb</i> climates are also encountered at high elevations in certain subtropical and tropical areas, where the climate would be that of a subtropical/tropical rain forest if not for the altitude. These climates are called "highlands".<sup id="cite_ref-McKnight_9-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-McKnight-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>226–9</span></sup>
</p><p><b>Examples</b>

<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Subtropical_highland_climate_with_uniform_rainfall">Subtropical highland climate with uniform rainfall</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Subtropical highland climate with uniform rainfall">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Oceanic_climate#Subtropical_highland_variety_(Cfb,_Cwb)" title="Oceanic climate">Oceanic climate §&#160;Subtropical highland variety (Cfb, Cwb)</a></div>
<p>Subtropical highland climates with uniform rainfall (<i>Cfb</i>) are a type of oceanic climate mainly found in highlands of <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a>, such as in or around the <a href="/wiki/Great_Dividing_Range" title="Great Dividing Range">Great Dividing Range</a> in the states of <a href="/wiki/New_South_Wales" title="New South Wales">New South Wales</a> and <a href="/wiki/Victoria_(state)" class="mw-redirect" title="Victoria (state)">Victoria</a>, and also sparsely in other continents, such as in <a href="/wiki/South_America" title="South America">South America</a>, among others. Unlike a typical <i>Cwb</i> climate, they tend to have rainfall spread evenly throughout the year. They have characteristics of both the <i>Cfb</i> and <i>Cfa</i> climates, but unlike these climates, they have a high <a href="/wiki/Diurnal_temperature_variation" title="Diurnal temperature variation">diurnal temperature variation</a> and low humidity, owing to their inland location and relatively high <a href="/wiki/Elevation" title="Elevation">elevation</a>.
</p><p><b>Examples</b>
</p>
<div>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cfc:_Subpolar_oceanic_climate"><i>Cfc</i>: Subpolar oceanic climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Cfc: Subpolar oceanic climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Subpolar oceanic climates (<i>Cfc</i>) occur poleward of or at higher elevations than the maritime temperate climates, and are mostly confined either to narrow coastal strips on the western poleward margins of the continents, or, especially in the Northern Hemisphere, to islands off such coasts. They occur in both hemispheres, most often at latitudes from 60° north and south to 70° north and south.<sup id="cite_ref-McKnight_9-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-McKnight-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><b>Examples</b>
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Reykjav%C3%ADk" title="Reykjavík">Reykjavík</a>, <a href="/wiki/Iceland" title="Iceland">Iceland</a> (<i>Cfc</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/T%C3%B3rshavn" title="Tórshavn">Tórshavn</a>, <a href="/wiki/Faroe_Islands" title="Faroe Islands">Faroe Islands</a> (<i>Cfc</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/R%C3%B8st" title="Røst">Røst</a>, <a href="/wiki/Norway" title="Norway">Norway</a> (<i>Cfc</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bod%C3%B8" title="Bodø">Bodø</a>, Norway (<i>Cfc</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Miena,_Tasmania" title="Miena, Tasmania">Miena</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tasmania" title="Tasmania">Tasmania</a>, <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a> (<i>Cfc</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Charlotte_Pass,_New_South_Wales" title="Charlotte Pass, New South Wales">Charlotte Pass</a>, Australia (<i>Cfc</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Auckland_Islands" title="Auckland Islands">Auckland Islands</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">New Zealand</a> (<i>Cfc</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Punta_Arenas" title="Punta Arenas">Punta Arenas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chile" title="Chile">Chile</a> (<i>Cfc</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/R%C3%ADo_Grande,_Tierra_del_Fuego" title="Río Grande, Tierra del Fuego">Río Grande</a>, <a href="/wiki/Argentina" title="Argentina">Argentina</a> (<i>Cfc</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/R%C3%ADo_Turbio" title="Río Turbio">Río Turbio</a>, Argentina (<i>Cfc</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Unalaska,_Alaska" title="Unalaska, Alaska">Unalaska</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alaska" title="Alaska">Alaska</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> (<i>Cfc</i>)</li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cwa:_Dry-winter_humid_subtropical_climate"><i>Cwa</i>: Dry-winter humid subtropical climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Cwa: Dry-winter humid subtropical climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><i>Cwa</i> is monsoonal influenced, having the classic dry winter – wet summer pattern associated with tropical monsoonal climates.

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cwb:_Dry-winter_subtropical_highland_climate"><i>Cwb</i>: Dry-winter subtropical highland climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Cwb: Dry-winter subtropical highland climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Dry-winter subtropical highland climate (<i>Cwb</i>) is a type of climate mainly found in highlands inside the tropics of <a href="/wiki/Central_America" title="Central America">Central America</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_America" title="South America">South America</a>, <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">Africa</a> and <a href="/wiki/Asia" title="Asia">Asia</a> or areas in the subtropics. Winters are noticeable and dry, and summers can be very rainy. In the tropics, the rainy season is provoked by the tropical air masses and the dry winters by subtropical high pressure.
</p><p><b>Examples</b>
</p>
<div>
<div>

&#32;
<table class="multicol" role="presentation" style="border-collapse: collapse; padding: 0; border: 0; background:transparent; width:70%;"><tbody><tr>
<td style="width: 50%;text-align: left; vertical-align: top;">
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Da_Lat" title="Da Lat">Da Lat</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vietnam" title="Vietnam">Vietnam</a> (<i>Cwb</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Gangtok" title="Gangtok">Gangtok</a>, <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a> (<i>Cwb</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ooty" title="Ooty">Ooty</a>, India (<i>Cwb</i>)</li>

</p>
</td></tr></tbody></table></div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cwc:_Dry-winter_subpolar_oceanic_climate"><i>Cwc</i>: Dry-winter subpolar oceanic climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Cwc: Dry-winter subpolar oceanic climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Found located mainly above <i>Cwb</i> climates, it is found mainly in isolated locations mostly in the Andes in Bolivia, Peru and Argentina, as well as in sparse mountain locations in Southeast Asia. It is not common.
</p>
<div>
<div>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/El_Alto" title="El Alto">El Alto</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bolivia" title="Bolivia">Bolivia</a> (<i>Cwc</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Puno" title="Puno">Puno</a>, <a href="/wiki/Peru" title="Peru">Peru</a> (<i>Cwc</i>)</li></ul>
&#32;
<table class="multicol" role="presentation" style="border-collapse: collapse; padding: 0; border: 0; background:transparent; width:70%;">
<tbody><tr><td></td></tr></tbody></table></div>
</div>
<h2><span id="Group_D:_Continental.2Fmicrothermal_climates"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Group_D:_Continental/microthermal_climates">Group D: Continental/microthermal climates</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Group D: Continental/microthermal climates">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Continental_climate" title="Continental climate">Continental climate</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Odori_Park_Sapporo_Snow_Festival_2007.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Odori_Park_Sapporo_Snow_Festival_2007.JPG/220px-Odori_Park_Sapporo_Snow_Festival_2007.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="330" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Odori_Park_Sapporo_Snow_Festival_2007.JPG/330px-Odori_Park_Sapporo_Snow_Festival_2007.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Odori_Park_Sapporo_Snow_Festival_2007.JPG/440px-Odori_Park_Sapporo_Snow_Festival_2007.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2260" data-file-height="3390" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Odori_Park_Sapporo_Snow_Festival_2007.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The snowy city of <a href="/wiki/Sapporo" title="Sapporo">Sapporo</a></div></div></div>
<p>These climates have an average temperature above 10&#160;°C (50&#160;°F) in their warmest months, and a coldest month average below 0&#160;°C (or −3&#160;°C (27&#160;°F), as noted previously). These usually occur in the interiors of continents and on their upper east coasts, normally north of 40°N. In the Southern Hemisphere, group D climates are extremely rare due to the smaller land masses in the middle latitudes and the almost complete absence of land at 40–60°S, existing only in some highland locations.
</p>
<h3><span id="Dfa.2FDwa.2FDsa:_Hot_summer_continental_climates"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Dfa/Dwa/Dsa:_Hot_summer_continental_climates"><i>Dfa/Dwa/Dsa</i>: Hot summer continental climates</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Dfa/Dwa/Dsa: Hot summer continental climates">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Hot-summer_humid_continental_climate" class="mw-redirect" title="Hot-summer humid continental climate">Hot-summer humid continental climate</a></div>
<p><i>Dfa</i> climates usually occur in the high 30s and low 40s latitudes, with a qualifying average temperature in the warmest month of greater than 22&#160;°C/72&#160;°F. In Europe, these climates tend to be much drier than in North America. <i>Dsa</i> exists at higher elevations adjacent to areas with hot summer Mediterranean (<i>Csa</i>) climates.<sup id="cite_ref-McKnight_9-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-McKnight-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>231–2</span></sup>
</p><p>These climates exist only in the northern hemisphere because the southern hemisphere has no locations that get the combination of hot summers and snowy winters because the southern hemisphere has no  large landmasses isolated from the moderating effects of the sea within the 
upper-middle latitudes. 
</p><p><b>Examples</b>
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Almaty" title="Almaty">Almaty</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kazakhstan" title="Kazakhstan">Kazakhstan</a> (<i>Dfa</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Oral,_Kazakhstan" title="Oral, Kazakhstan">Oral</a>, Kazakhstan (<i>Dfa</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Aomori,_Aomori" class="mw-redirect" title="Aomori, Aomori">Aomori</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aomori_Prefecture" title="Aomori Prefecture">Aomori Prefecture</a>, <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">Japan</a> (<i>Dfa</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Nagano,_Nagano" class="mw-redirect" title="Nagano, Nagano">Nagano</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nagano_Prefecture" title="Nagano Prefecture">Nagano Prefecture</a>, Japan (<i>Dfa</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Sapporo" title="Sapporo">Sapporo</a>, Japan (<i>Dfa</i>, bordering on <i>Dfb</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Chicago" title="Chicago">Chicago</a>, <a href="/wiki/Illinois" title="Illinois">Illinois</a>, United States (<i>Dfa</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Boston,_Massachusetts" class="mw-redirect" title="Boston, Massachusetts">Boston, Massachusetts</a>, United States (<i>Dfa</i>, bordering on <i>Cfa</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Minneapolis" title="Minneapolis">Minneapolis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Minnesota" title="Minnesota">Minnesota</a>, United States (<i>Dfa</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Toronto" title="Toronto">Toronto</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ontario" title="Ontario">Ontario</a>, Canada (<i>Dfa</i>, bordering on <i>Dfb</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Montreal,_Quebec" class="mw-redirect" title="Montreal, Quebec">Montreal, Quebec</a>, Canada (<i>Dfa</i>, bordering on <i>Dfb</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Windsor,_Ontario" title="Windsor, Ontario">Windsor, Ontario</a>, Canada (<i>Dfa</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bucharest" title="Bucharest">Bucharest</a>, <a href="/wiki/Romania" title="Romania">Romania</a> (<i>Dfa</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Rostov-on-Don" title="Rostov-on-Don">Rostov-on-Don</a>, <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a> (<i>Dfa</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Volgograd" title="Volgograd">Volgograd</a>, Russia (<i>Dfa</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Dnipro" title="Dnipro">Dnipro</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine">Ukraine</a> (<i>Dfa, bordering on </i>Dfb<i>)</i></li></ul>
<p>In eastern Asia, <i>Dwa</i> climates extend further south due to the influence of the Siberian high pressure system, which also causes winters there to be dry, and summers can be very wet because of <a href="/wiki/Monsoon" title="Monsoon">monsoon</a> circulation.
</p><p><b>Examples</b>
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Pyongyang" title="Pyongyang">Pyongyang</a>, <a href="/wiki/North_Korea" title="North Korea">North Korea</a> (<i>Dwa</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Seoul" title="Seoul">Seoul</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_Korea" title="South Korea">South Korea</a> (<i>Dwa</i>, Bordering on <i>Cwa</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Beijing" title="Beijing">Beijing</a>, <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a> (<i>Dwa</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Harbin" title="Harbin">Harbin</a>, China (<i>Dwa</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/North_Platte,_Nebraska" title="North Platte, Nebraska">North Platte</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nebraska" title="Nebraska">Nebraska</a>, United States (<i>Dwa</i>)</li></ul>
<p><i>Dsa</i> exists only at higher elevations adjacent to areas with hot summer Mediterranean (<i>Csa</i>) climates.
</p><p><b>Examples</b>
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Bishkek" title="Bishkek">Bishkek</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kyrgyzstan" title="Kyrgyzstan">Kyrgyzstan</a> (<i>Dsa</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Salmas" title="Salmas">Salmas</a>, <a href="/wiki/West_Azerbaijan_Province" title="West Azerbaijan Province">West Azerbaijan Province</a>, <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iran</a> (<i>Dsa</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Saqqez" title="Saqqez">Saqqez</a>, Kurdistan Province, Iran (<i>Dsa</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Hakk%C3%A2ri" title="Hakkâri">Hakkâri</a>, <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a> (<i>Dsa</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Mu%C5%9F" title="Muş">Muş</a>, Turkey (<i>Dsa</i>)</li></ul>
<h3><span id="Dfb.2FDwb.2FDsb:_Warm_summer_continental_or_hemiboreal_climates"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Dfb/Dwb/Dsb:_Warm_summer_continental_or_hemiboreal_climates"><i>Dfb/Dwb/Dsb</i>: Warm summer continental or hemiboreal climates</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Dfb/Dwb/Dsb: Warm summer continental or hemiboreal climates">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Warm-summer_humid_continental_climate" class="mw-redirect" title="Warm-summer humid continental climate">Warm-summer humid continental climate</a></div>
<p><i>Dfb</i> climates are immediately poleward of hot summer continental climates, generally in the high 40s and low 50s latitudes in North America and Asia, and also extending to higher latitudes in central and eastern Europe and Russia, between the maritime temperate and continental subarctic climates, where it extends up to 65 degrees latitude in places.<sup id="cite_ref-McKnight_9-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-McKnight-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><b><i>Dfb</i> examples</b>
</p>
<div>
<div>

<li><a href="/wiki/Warsaw" title="Warsaw">Warsaw</a>, <a href="/wiki/Poland" title="Poland">Poland</a> (<i>Dfb</i>)</li>
