<p><b><i>Dwb</i> examples</b>
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Calgary" title="Calgary">Calgary</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alberta" title="Alberta">Alberta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a> (<i>Dwb</i>, bordering on <i>Dfb</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Heihe" title="Heihe">Heihe</a>, <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a> (<i>Dwb</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Vladivostok" title="Vladivostok">Vladivostok</a>, <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a> (<i>Dwb</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Irkutsk" title="Irkutsk">Irkutsk</a>, Russia (<i>Dwb</i>, bordering on <i>Dwc</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Baruunturuun" title="Baruunturuun">Baruunturuun</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mongolia" title="Mongolia">Mongolia</a> (<i>Dwb</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Pyeongchang_County" title="Pyeongchang County">Pyeongchang County</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_Korea" title="South Korea">South Korea</a> (<i>Dwb</i>, bordering on <i>Dfb</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Pembina,_North_Dakota" title="Pembina, North Dakota">Pembina, North Dakota</a>, United States (<i>Dwb</i>)</li></ul>
<p><i>Dsb</i> arises from the same scenario as <i>Dsa</i>, but at even higher altitudes or latitudes, and chiefly in North America, since the Mediterranean climates extend further poleward than in Eurasia.
</p><p><b>Examples</b>
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Sivas" title="Sivas">Sivas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a> (<i>Dsb</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Roghun" title="Roghun">Roghun</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tajikistan" title="Tajikistan">Tajikistan</a> (<i>Dsb</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Dras" title="Dras">Dras</a>, <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a> (<i>Dsb</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Flagstaff,_Arizona" title="Flagstaff, Arizona">Flagstaff</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arizona" title="Arizona">Arizona</a>, United States (<i>Dsb</i>)</li></ul>
<h3><span id="Dfc.2FDwc.2FDsc:_Subarctic_or_boreal_climates"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Dfc/Dwc/Dsc:_Subarctic_or_boreal_climates"><i>Dfc/Dwc/Dsc</i>: Subarctic or boreal climates</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Dfc/Dwc/Dsc: Subarctic or boreal climates">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Subarctic_climate" title="Subarctic climate">Subarctic climate</a></div>
<p><i>Dfc</i>, <i>Dsc</i> and <i>Dwc</i> climates occur poleward of the other group D climates, or at higher altitudes, generally between the 55° to 65° North latitudes, occasionally reaching up to the 70°N latitude.<sup id="cite_ref-McKnight_9-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-McKnight-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>232–5</span></sup>
</p><p><b>Examples</b>:
</p>
<div>
<div>

&#32;
<table class="multicol" role="presentation" style="border-collapse: collapse; padding: 0; border: 0; background:transparent; width:70%;"><tbody><tr>
<td style="width: 50%;text-align: left; vertical-align: top;">
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Yellowknife" title="Yellowknife">Yellowknife</a>, <a href="/wiki/Northwest_Territories" title="Northwest Territories">Northwest Territories</a>, <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a> (<i>Dfc</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Thompson,_Manitoba" title="Thompson, Manitoba">Thompson, Manitoba</a>, Canada (<i>Dfc</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Labrador_City" title="Labrador City">Labrador City</a>, <a href="/wiki/Newfoundland_and_Labrador" title="Newfoundland and Labrador">Newfoundland and Labrador</a>, Canada (<i>Dfc</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Fairbanks,_Alaska" title="Fairbanks, Alaska">Fairbanks</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alaska" title="Alaska">Alaska</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> (<i>Dfc</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Fraser,_Colorado" title="Fraser, Colorado">Fraser</a>, <a href="/wiki/Colorado" title="Colorado">Colorado</a>, United States (<i>Dfc</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Saint_Pierre_and_Miquelon" title="Saint Pierre and Miquelon">Saint Pierre and Miquelon</a>, <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a> (<i>Dfc</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Oulu" title="Oulu">Oulu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Finland" title="Finland">Finland</a> (<i>Dfc</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Tampere" title="Tampere">Tampere</a>, Finland (<i>Dfc, bordering on Dfb</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Lule%C3%A5" title="Luleå">Luleå</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sweden" title="Sweden">Sweden</a> (<i>Dfc</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Arkhangelsk" title="Arkhangelsk">Arkhangelsk</a>, Russia (<i>Dfc</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Norilsk" title="Norilsk">Norilsk</a>, Russia (<i>Dfc</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Troms%C3%B8" title="Tromsø">Tromsø</a>, <a href="/wiki/Norway" title="Norway">Norway</a> (<i>Dfc</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/St._Moritz" title="St. Moritz">St. Moritz</a>, <a href="/wiki/Grisons" title="Grisons">Grisons</a>, <a href="/wiki/Switzerland" title="Switzerland">Switzerland</a> (<i>Dfc</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Livigno" title="Livigno">Livigno</a>, <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a> (<i>Dfc</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Kangerlussuaq" title="Kangerlussuaq">Kangerlussuaq</a>, <a href="/wiki/Greenland" title="Greenland">Greenland</a> (<i>Dfc</i>)</li></ul>
<p>&#32;
</p>
</td>
<td style="width: 50%;text-align: left; vertical-align: top;">
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Anchorage,_Alaska" title="Anchorage, Alaska">Anchorage</a>, Alaska, United States (<i>Dsc</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Brian_Head,_Utah" title="Brian Head, Utah">Brian Head</a>, <a href="/wiki/Utah" title="Utah">Utah</a>, United States (<i>Dsc</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Whitehorse,_Yukon" title="Whitehorse, Yukon">Whitehorse</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yukon" title="Yukon">Yukon</a>, Canada (<i>Dsc</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Kuujjuarapik" title="Kuujjuarapik">Kuujjuarapik</a>, <a href="/wiki/Quebec" title="Quebec">Quebec</a>, Canada (<i>Dsc</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Nyurba" title="Nyurba">Nyurba</a>, Russia (<i>Dsc, bordering on Dsd</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Anadyr_(town)" title="Anadyr (town)">Anadyr</a>, Russia (<i>Dsc</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Skj%C3%A5k" title="Skjåk">Skjåk</a>, Norway (<i>Dsc</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Chita,_Zabaykalsky_Krai" title="Chita, Zabaykalsky Krai">Chita</a>, Russia (<i>Dwc</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Mohe_County" class="mw-redirect" title="Mohe County">Mohe County</a>, <a href="/wiki/Heilongjiang" title="Heilongjiang">Heilongjiang</a>, China (<i>Dwc</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Yushu_City,_Qinghai" title="Yushu City, Qinghai">Yushu City</a>, <a href="/wiki/Qinghai" title="Qinghai">Qinghai</a>, China (<i>Dwc</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Lukla" title="Lukla">Lukla</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nepal" title="Nepal">Nepal</a> (<i>Dwc</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Delta_Junction" class="mw-redirect" title="Delta Junction">Delta Junction</a>, Alaska, United States (<i>Dwc</i>)</li></ul>
<p>&#32;
</p>
</td></tr></tbody></table></div>
</div>
<h3><span id="Dfd.2FDwd.2FDsd:_Subarctic_or_boreal_climates_with_severe_winters"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Dfd/Dwd/Dsd:_Subarctic_or_boreal_climates_with_severe_winters"><i>Dfd/Dwd/Dsd</i>: Subarctic or boreal climates with severe winters</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Dfd/Dwd/Dsd: Subarctic or boreal climates with severe winters">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Places with this climate have severe winters, with the temperature in their coldest month lower than −38&#160;°C. These climates occur only in eastern <a href="/wiki/Siberia" title="Siberia">Siberia</a>. The names of some of the places with this climate have become veritable synonyms for extreme, severe winter cold.
</p><p><b>Examples</b>
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Yakutsk" title="Yakutsk">Yakutsk</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sakha_Republic" class="mw-redirect" title="Sakha Republic">Sakha Republic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a> (<i>Dfd</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Oymyakon" title="Oymyakon">Oymyakon</a>, Sakha Republic, Russia (<i>Dfd, bordering on Dwd</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Verkhoyansk" title="Verkhoyansk">Verkhoyansk</a>, Sakha Republic, Russia (<i>Dfd</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Allakh-Yun" title="Allakh-Yun">Allakh-Yun</a>, Sakha Republic, Russia (<i>Dwd</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Zhigansk" title="Zhigansk">Zhigansk</a>, Sakha Republic, Russia (<i>Dsd, bordering on Dfd</i>)</li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Group_E:_Polar_climates">Group E: Polar climates</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Group E: Polar climates">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>In the Köppen climate system, polar climates are defined as the warmest temperature of any month is below 10&#160;°C (50&#160;°F). Polar climates are further divided into two types, tundra climates and icecap climates:
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="ET:_Tundra_climate"><i>ET</i>: Tundra climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: ET: Tundra climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><b><a href="/wiki/Tundra" title="Tundra">Tundra</a> climate</b> (<i>ET</i>): Warmest month has an average temperature between 0 and 10&#160;°C. These climates occur on the northern edges of the North American and Eurasian land masses (generally north of 70 °N although it may be found farther south depending on local conditions), and on nearby islands. <i>ET</i> climates are also found on some islands near the Antarctic Convergence, and at high elevations outside the polar regions, above the tree line.
</p><p><b>Examples</b>
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Mount_Rainier,_Washington" class="mw-redirect" title="Mount Rainier, Washington">Mount Rainier</a>, Washington, United States (<i>ET</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Macquarie_Island" title="Macquarie Island">Macquarie Island</a>, Australia (<i>ET</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Crozet_Islands" title="Crozet Islands">Crozet Islands</a> (<i>ET</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Campbell_Island,_New_Zealand" title="Campbell Island, New Zealand">Campbell Island</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">New Zealand</a> (<i>ET</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Kerguelen_Islands" title="Kerguelen Islands">Kerguelen Islands</a> (<i>ET</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Prince_Edwards_Islands" class="mw-redirect" title="Prince Edwards Islands">Prince Edwards Islands</a> (<i>ET</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Stanley,_Falkland_Islands" title="Stanley, Falkland Islands">Stanley</a>, <a href="/wiki/Falkland_Islands" title="Falkland Islands">Falkland Islands</a> (<i>ET</i>), borders subpolar oceanic (<i>Cfc</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ushuaia" title="Ushuaia">Ushuaia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Argentina" title="Argentina">Argentina</a> (<i>ET</i>), (borders on <i>Cfc</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Mount_Wellington_(Tasmania)" title="Mount Wellington (Tasmania)">Mount Wellington</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tasmania" title="Tasmania">Tasmania</a>, <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a> (<i>ET</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Mykines,_Mykines" title="Mykines, Mykines">Mykines</a>, <a href="/wiki/Faroe_Islands" title="Faroe Islands">Faroe Islands</a> (<i>ET</i>), (borders on <i>Cfc</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ben_Nevis" title="Ben Nevis">Ben Nevis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Scotland" title="Scotland">Scotland</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a> (<i>ET</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Cairn_Gorm" title="Cairn Gorm">Cairn Gorm</a>, <a href="/wiki/Scotland" title="Scotland">Scotland</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a> (<i>ET</i>)</li></ul>
<p>These <i>ET</i> climates are a colder and more continental variants of tundra. They would have characteristics of the ice cap climate, but still manage to see monthly average temperatures above 0&#160;°C (32&#160;°F):
</p><p><b>Examples</b>
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Mount_Fuji" title="Mount Fuji">Mount Fuji</a>, Japan (<i>ET</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Murghab,_Tajikistan" title="Murghab, Tajikistan">Murghab, Tajikistan</a> (<i>ET</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Mount_Washington,_New_Hampshire" class="mw-redirect" title="Mount Washington, New Hampshire">Mount Washington</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_Hampshire" title="New Hampshire">New Hampshire</a>, United States (<i>ET</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Zugspitze" title="Zugspitze">Zugspitze</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bavaria" title="Bavaria">Bavaria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a> (<i>ET</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Eureka,_Nunavut" title="Eureka, Nunavut">Eureka, Nunavut</a>, Canada (<i>ET</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Iqaluit,_Nunavut" class="mw-redirect" title="Iqaluit, Nunavut">Iqaluit, Nunavut</a>, Canada (<i>ET</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Inukjuak,_Quebec" class="mw-redirect" title="Inukjuak, Quebec">Inukjuak, Quebec</a>, Canada (<i>ET</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Nuuk,_Greenland" class="mw-redirect" title="Nuuk, Greenland">Nuuk</a>, <a href="/wiki/Greenland" title="Greenland">Greenland</a> (<i>ET</i>, bordering on <i>Dfc</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Svalbard" title="Svalbard">Svalbard</a>, <a href="/wiki/Norway" title="Norway">Norway</a> (<i>ET</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Mys_Shmidta" title="Mys Shmidta">Mys Shmidta</a>, Russia (<i>ET</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Dikson_Island" title="Dikson Island">Dikson Island</a>, Russia (<i>ET</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Nord,_Greenland" class="mw-redirect" title="Nord, Greenland">Nord</a>, Greenland (<i>ET</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Esperanza_Base" title="Esperanza Base">Esperanza Base</a>, <a href="/wiki/Antarctica" title="Antarctica">Antarctica</a> (<i>ET</i>)</li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="EF:_Ice_cap_climate"><i>EF</i>: Ice cap climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: EF: Ice cap climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><b><a href="/wiki/Ice_cap_climate" title="Ice cap climate">Ice cap climate</a></b> (<i>EF</i>): This climate is dominant in Antarctica and inner Greenland, but also occurs at extremely high altitudes on mountains, above even tundra. Monthly average temperatures never exceed 0&#160;°C (32&#160;°F).
</p><p><b>Examples</b>
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Mount_Rainier" title="Mount Rainier">Mount Rainier</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> (<i>EF</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Mount_Ararat" title="Mount Ararat">Mount Ararat</a>, Turkey (<i>EF</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Grossglockner" title="Grossglockner">Grossglockner</a>, <a href="/wiki/Carinthia" title="Carinthia">Carinthia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Austria" title="Austria">Austria</a> (<i>EF</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Mount_Everest" title="Mount Everest">Mount Everest</a>, China/Nepal (<i>EF</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/K2" title="K2">K2</a>, China/Pakistan (<i>EF</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Summit_Camp" title="Summit Camp">Summit Camp</a>, Greenland (<i>EF</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/McMurdo_Station" title="McMurdo Station">McMurdo Station</a>, Antarctica (<i>EF</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Scott_Base" title="Scott Base">Scott Base</a>, <a href="/wiki/Antarctica" title="Antarctica">Antarctica</a> (<i>EF</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Byrd_Station" title="Byrd Station">Byrd Station</a>, Antarctica (<i>EF</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Amundsen%E2%80%93Scott_South_Pole_Station" title="Amundsen–Scott South Pole Station">Amundsen–Scott station</a>, Antarctica (<i>EF</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Vostok_Station" title="Vostok Station">Vostok Station</a>, Antarctica (<i>EF</i>), location of the lowest air temperature ever recorded on Earth.</li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Ecological_significance">Ecological significance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Ecological significance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The Köppen climate classification is based on the empirical relationship between climate and vegetation. This classification provides an efficient way to describe climatic conditions defined by temperature and precipitation and their seasonality with a single metric. Because climatic conditions identified by the Köppen classification are ecologically relevant, it has been widely used to map geographic distribution of long term climate and associated ecosystem conditions.<sup id="cite_ref-Chen_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chen-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Over the recent years, there has been an increasing interest in using the classification to identify changes in climate and potential changes in vegetation over time.<sup id="cite_ref-hanschen_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hanschen-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> The most important ecological significance of the Köppen climate classification is that it helps to predict the dominant vegetation type based on the climatic data and vice versa.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2015, a <a href="/wiki/Nanjing_University" title="Nanjing University">Nanjing University</a> paper published in <i><a href="/wiki/Nature_(journal)" title="Nature (journal)">Nature</a></i> analyzing climate classifications found that between 1950 and 2010, approximately 5.7% of all land area worldwide had moved from wetter and colder classifications to drier and hotter classifications. The authors also found that the change "cannot be explained as natural variations but are driven by anthropogenic factors."<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span id="Other_K.C3.B6ppen_climate_maps"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_Köppen_climate_maps">Other Köppen climate maps</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Other Köppen climate maps">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>All maps use the ≥0&#160;°C definition for temperate climates and the 18&#160;°C annual mean temperature threshold to distinguish between hot and cold dry climates.<sup id="cite_ref-Beck_1-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Beck-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Holdridge_life_zones" title="Holdridge life zones">Holdridge life zones</a>, climate classification by three dimensions: precipitation, humidity, and potential evapotranspiration ratio</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Trewartha_climate_classification" title="Trewartha climate classification">Trewartha climate classification</a> scheme by American geographer Glenn Thomas Trewartha in 1966 and updated in 1980, based on the Köppen scheme</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Savory_brittleness_scale" title="Savory brittleness scale">Savory brittleness scale</a></li>
